Jamison Brereton

58
Agni
Nodhas Gautama
9 verses: jagat─л 1тАУ5, triс╣гс╣нubh 6тАУ9
Although Nodhas GautamaтАЩs poetic intricacy is not as much on display in his Agni hymns as in his Indra hymns, he excels here in his vivid and dense depiction of physical fire, especially the forest fire. In the jagat─л portion of the hymn, verses con cerning ritual fire (1, 3) alternate with evocations of the unchecked passage of fire in the woods (2, 4тАУ5), while the final four verses (6тАУ9), in triс╣гс╣нubh, are only about the ritual fire. The ritual verses focus on the choosing and installation of Agni as Hotar (vss. 1, 3, 6тАУ7), especially in its first enactment by the gods and the human ancestors (see esp. vss. 3, 6).
The counterpoint between wild uncontrollable fire and ritual fire may subtly emphasize what a feat of civilizing was accomplished by taming fire for sacrificial (and domestic) purposes in the legendary past, and how this feat is repeated in the present day. The last two verses (8тАУ9) beg Agni for shelter and protection for us, the singers. Again, the image of a guardian fire may acquire special intensity by contrast with the potentially destructive fire in the wild.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe strength-genitive rated, immortal Agni quickly issues forth, when he is the invoker of the gods, and the messenger (of the worshipper) (then proceeding) by suitable paths, he has made the firmament, and worships (the deities) in the sacrifice with oblationс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Agni is identified with light; firmament existed in darkness and agni made it visible; hence agni is said to have created (vimame, nirmame) the firmamement

Jamison Brereton

Never is the immortal one, born of strength, forced down. When he became Hotar, messenger of Vivasvant,
he measured across the airy realm along the paths that lead straightest to the goal. In service to the gods he entices them here with the
oblation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Phonetic figure spanning the end of the first hemistich and the second (esp. its end): … viv├бsvataс╕е# #v├н … , … hav├нс╣г─Б viv─Бsati# The lexeme n├н тИЪtud is generally taken to mean something like тАШspur onтАЩ, but that tr. fails to render the n├н. I prefer to take it in the literal sense тАШpush down, force downтАЩ, meaning that, in the English idiom, you canтАЩt keep Agni down.

I connect p─Бda b with c, rather than with a, as the standard tr. do, because of the difference in tense (pres. n├н tundate, impf. ├бbhavat). This tense mismatch requires the y├бd of b to have the sense тАЬever sinceтАЭ (Geldner[/Witzel Got┼Н] тАЬseitdem,тАЭ Renou тАЬdepuis queтАЭ), which does not seem to me to be natural to it. By contrast, AgniтАЩs assuming the office of messenger in b leads directly to his journey in c.

Griffith

NE’ER waxeth faint the Immortal, Son of Strength, since he, the Herald, hath become Vivasvan’s messenger.
On paths most excellent he measured out mid-air: he with oblation calls to service of the Gods.

Oldenberg

Seizing his own food the undecaying, greedy (Agni) stands on the brushwood wishing to drink. When he has been sprinkled (with ghee), he shines like a racer with his back 1. Thundering he has roared like the ridge of heaven.

Geldner

Niemals wird der kraftgeborene Unsterbliche angestachelt, seitdem er der Hotri und Bote des Vivasvat wurde. Auf den richtigsten Wegen hat er den Raum durchschritten; er bittet die G├╢tter durch die Opferspende zum Gottesdienst her.

Grassmann

Stets dringt der kraftgeborne ein, der nimmer stirbt, weil des Vivasvat Priester er und Bote ward; Die Luft durchmisst auf ganz geraden Pfaden er, und ladet ein zum G├╢tterfest durch Opferguss.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUndecaying Agni, combining his food (with his flame), and devouring it quickly, ascends the dry wood; the blaze of theconsuming (element) spreads like a (fleet) courser, and roars like a roaring (cloud) in the height of heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Adma = food or what may be eaten, explained as tс╣Ыс╣Зagulm─Бdiam, straw and twigs;

Atasa = k─Бс╣гс╣нha, wood or timber

Jamison Brereton

The unaging one, drawing his own food toward him, thirstily eager to eat, keeps to the thickets.
His back when he is sprinkled shines like a steed; thundering like the spine of heaven, he has roared.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b tiс╣гс╣нhati can mean, as I take it, тАЬstays (within)тАЭ or, with Geldner, тАЬstands up (in).тАЭ In the latter case, the image would be of a forest fire, fed by brush, flaring up.

This is possible, but in the absence of the preverb ├║d or similar directional indications, I prefer the former.

Griffith

Never decaying, seizing his appropriate food, rapidly, eagerly through the dry wood he spreads.
His back, as he is sprinkled, glistens like a horse: loud hath he roared and shouted like the heights of heaven?

Geldner

Seine eigene Speise h├дlt der Alterlose fest; in den Str├дuchern steht er auf, gierig nach Nahrung verlangend. Wie eines Hengstes ergl├дnzt sein R├╝cken, wenn er mit Schmalz betropft wird. Donnernd wie des Himmels W├╢lbung hat er sein Gebr├╝ll erhoben.

Grassmann

Der ewig junge, an sich reissend seinen Frass, geht voll Begierde, l├╝stern zu den H├╢lzern hin, Es gl├дnzt der R├╝cken des benetzten wie ein Ross, und wie des Himmels Gipfel schrie er donnernd auf.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe immortal, and resplendent Agni, the bearer of oblations, honoured by the Rudras and the Vasus the invoker of the gods, who presides over oblations and is the distributor of riches, praised by his worshippers, and admired like a chariot amongst mankind, accepts the oblations that are successively presented.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purohitaс╕е = puraskс╣Ыtaс╕е, honoured or lit. plural ced in front or preceding

Jamison Brereton

He was placed in front successfully by the Rudras and the Vasus, set down as Hotar, the immortal who conquers wealth,
like a chariot steering straight among the clans descended from ─Аyu. The god discloses valuables in due order.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On kr─Бс╣З─Б╠БтАШsuccessfullyтАЩ, derived from the old fem. instr. sg. of the med. root aor. participle of тИЪkс╣Ы in adv. usage, see Oldenberg (Fs. Kern [1903] 33-36 = KlSch 1111- 14 [details in EWA s.v. kс╣Ы─Бс╣З─Б╠Б]).

Since v├н / ├бpa + с╣Ыс╣З├│ti/с╣Ыс╣Зv├бti regularly refers to the unclosing of doors and the like (e.g., I.128.6 dv─Б╠Бr─Б vy с╣Ы╠Ас╣Зvati; IX.102.8 с╣Ыс╣З├│r ├бpa vraj├бm), the tr. тАШdistributeтАЩ (Geldner тАШteilt тАж ausтАЩ, Witzel Got┼Н тАШverteiltтАЩ, Renou тАШr├йpartitтАЩ) seriously manipulates the idiom. I therefore prefer тАШdiscloseтАЩ - that is, unclose and reveal to sight. (So also Oldenberg SBE.) In this usage the stem has clearly assimilated itself to ┼лrс╣Зoti (тИЪvс╣Ы) + ├бpa / v├н тАШopenтАЩ, and one wonders if they were felt to belong to different roots by the poets. For further on this stem see K├╝mmel 104-5.

Griffith

Set high in place o’er all that Vasus, Rudras do, immortal, Lord of riches, seated as High Priest;
Hastening like a car to men, to those who live, the God without delay gives boons to be desired.

Oldenberg

As soon as 1 the Rudras, the Vasus have made him their Purohita, the immortal sitting down as Hotri, the conqueror of wealth, pressing forward like a chariot among the clans, among the ├Вyus 2, the god in due course discloses desirable boons.

Geldner

Im Zusammenwirken von den Rudra┬┤s, den Vasu┬┤s bevollm├дchtigt und als Hotri eingesetzt, der an Reichtum ├╝berlegene Unsterbliche, hat er wie ein Wagen unter den Ayuclanen den Vorrang. Der Gott teilt w├╝nschenswerte Gaben nach der Ordnung aus.

Grassmann

Mit Rudra’s, Vasu’s wirkt als Hauses Opfrer er, als ew’ger Priester, Schatz gewinnend, sitzet er, Zu H├дusern, Menschen wie ein Wagen eilt er hin, der Gott erschliesset sch├╢nes Gut der Reihe nach.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

Impelled ahead by the wind, he stands among the shrubbery,
effortlessly, with flames [like] a sickle, making a great noise.
Greedily, when, O agni, you bullishly rush at the trees,
Black is your path, O you, with a blazing wave, O ageless one.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExcited by the wind, and roaring loudly, Agni penetrates easily with his flames and diffusive (intensity) among the timber; when, undecaying and fiercely-blazing Agni, you rush rapidly like a bull amongst the forest trees, your path is blackened.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sped by the wind, he spreads himself out among the thickets at will, with his tongues as sickle, powerfully noisy.
When, Agni, thirstily you rush like a bull upon the woods, black is your course, o unaging one with gleaming waves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. r├║┼Ыad-┼лrme тАШo you possessing gleaming wavesтАЩ should, strictly speaking, not be accented. It may owe its accent to IV.7.9 krс╣гс╣З╠е ├бс╣Г te ├йma r├║┼Ыataс╕е pur├│ bh─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬBlack is your course, (though) you are gleaming; your light is in front,тАЭ with a gen. sg. part. r├║┼Ыataс╕е following an identical opening. (So tentatively Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions) Or perhaps as the first of two voc., in post-caesura position, it was felt to begin a new syntagm.

Griffith

Urged by the wind be spreads through dry wood as he lists, armed with his tongues for sickles, with a mighty roar.
Black is thy path, Agni, changeless, with glittering waves! when like a bull thou rushest eager to the trees.

Oldenberg

Stirred by the wind he spreads among the brushwood lightly, 1 (driven forward) by the sacrificial ladles, with his sickle 2, loudly roaring. When thou, O Agni, thirstily rushest on the wooden sticks like a bull 3, thy course, O never-aging god with fiery waves, becomes black 4.

Geldner

Vom Winde getrieben breitet er sich nach Lust in den Str├дuchern mit seinen sichelf├╢rmigen Zungen aus, laut brausend. Wenn du, Agni, auf die B├дume dich gierig wie ein Bulle st├╝rzest, so ist dein Weg schwarz, du Hellwogender, Alterloser.

Grassmann

Vom Wind getrieben eilt er rings zu dem Gestr├╝pp, mit Zungen rauschend, mit der Sichel voller Lust, Wenn gierig, Agni, wie ein Stier zum Holz du dringst, ist schwarz dein Weg, hellwogender, unsterblicher!

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe flame-weaponed and breeze-excited Agni, assailing the unexhaled moisture (of the trees), with all his strength, in a volume of fire, rushes triumphant (against all things) in the forest, like a bull, and all, whether stationary or moveable, are afraid of him as he flies along.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With scorching fangs, spurred by the wind he gusts down upon the wood, like a victorious buffalo upon the herd, advancing upon the imperishable airy realm in his full dimension. The still and the moving fear, and also the winged ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On sth─Бt├║с╕е (in the pair sth─Бt├║┼Ы car├бtham тАЬthe still and the movingтАЭ) as neut.

sg. to the -tar-stem (тЖР *-tс╣Ы╠Б) see AiG I.23, 301; III.204 and most recently Frotscher 2012. Tichy (1995: 71) rejects this explanation, but her alternative (a masc. nom. sg.

to a -tu-stem) breaks the tight rhetorical structure of this merism by pairing a masculine with a neuter (car├бtham). Thus, whatever phonological problems there may be in assuming an *-с╣Ы# > -ur# change (as opposed to *-с╣Ыs > -ur as in the gen. sg.

of -с╣Ы-stems), I favor the older view. FrotscherтАЩs suggestion that accented final -с╣Ы╠Б develops to -├║r may help solve the problem. In any case the nom./acc. neut form here would also be reinforced by the semantically identical genitive sg. phrase sth─Бth├║┼Ы ca … (j├бgata┼Ы ca (I.159.3, II.31.5).

Griffith

With teeth of flame, wind-driven, through the wood he speeds, triumphant like a bull among the herd of cows,
With bright strength roaming to the everlasting air: things fixed, things moving quake before him as he flies.

Oldenberg

He who has fiery jaws, stirred by the wind, blazes down on the forest 1 as a strong bull (rushes) on the herd. When he proceeds 2 with his stream of light to the imperishable atmosphere, then what is moveable and immoveable (and) the winged (birds) are afraid.

Mit Flammenz├дhnen windgetrieben schnauft er hin zum Holz wie zu der Heerde der gewalt’ge Stier, Mit seinem Licht hinwandernd zu dem ew’gen Raum; vor dem beschwingten bebet, was da geht und steht.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реЗрд╖реБ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рднреГрдЧрд╡рдГ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдорд╣рд░реНрд╖рдпрдГ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдп рдЬрдиреНрдордиреЗ рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрдВ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рди рд╢реЛрднрдирдВ рдзрдирдорд┐рд╡ рдЖ рджрдзреБрдГ рдЖрдзрд╛рдирд╕рдВрднрд╛рд░реЗрд╖реБ рдордиреНрддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдиреЗрди рд╕рдорд╕реНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН ред рдЬрдиреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддреБрдВ рд╕реБрд╢рдХрдВ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдореН рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рд╡рддреНрдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдореН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдирджреЗрд╢реЗрд╖реБ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛рд░рдореН ред рд╡рд░реЗрдгреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд░рдгреАрдпрдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди рд╢реЗрд╡рдореН ред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рдЦрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░реЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рджрдзреБрдГ ред рд▓рд┐рдЯрд┐ рдЙрд╕рд┐ тАШ рдЖрддреЛ рд▓реЛрдк рдЗрдЯрд┐ рдЪ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЖрдХрд╛рд░рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред тАШрдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрддрддреНрддрддрдХреНрд╖реБрдГрд╖реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдГрдкрд╛рджрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╕рд░реНрдЬрдиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╖рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рдореН ред рд╣реНрд╡рдпрддреЗрдГ ‘рдИрд╖рджреНрджреБрд╕реБрд╖реБ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЦрд▓реН ред тАЬ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рд░рдгрдореН ред рдкрд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдЧреБрдгрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреЗрд╢реМ ред тАШрд▓рд┐рддрд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╛рддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдХреГрджреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рддреНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Bhс╣Ыgus amongst men, for the sake of a divine birth, cherished you like a precious treasure Agni, who sacrifices for men, who are the invoker (of the gods), the (welcome) guest at sacrifices, and who are to be valued like an affectionate friend.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Divy─Бya janmane = for the sake of being born as gods

Jamison Brereton

The Bhr╠еgus installed you among the sons of Manu, dear like wealth, easy to invoke for the peoples,
as Hotar, o Agni, a guest worthy to be chosen, favorable like an ally to the divine race.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The last halves of the two hemistichs are parallel and complementary, referring to humans and gods respectively: b: тАж j├бnebhyaс╕е# / d: тАж divy─Б╠Бya j├бnmane# In c mitr├бm is of course ambiguous: it can refer simply to the god of that name (so Renou), but more likely is at least a pun on the meaning of the common noun тАШallyтАЩ. Agni is often so called because he serves as go-between between gods and men.

Griffith

The Bhrgus established thee among mankind for men, like as a treasure, beauteous, easy to invoke;
Thee, Agni, as a herald and choice-worthy guest, as an auspicious Friend to the Celestial Race.

Oldenberg

The Bhrigus have placed thee among men, who art beautiful like a treasure, who art easy to invoke for people; thee the Hotri, O Agni, the excellent guest, a delightful friend like Mitra to the divine race!

Geldner

Dich brachten die Bhrigu┬┤s zu den Menschen, der teuer wie ein Schatz, f├╝r die V├╢lker leicht zu errufen ist, als Hotri, o Agni, als auserw├дhlten Gast, wie ein Freund dem himmlischen Geschlecht lieb.

Grassmann

Die Bhrigu’s haben zu den Menschen dich gebracht, wie sch├╢nes Gut, leicht anzurufen jedem Mann, Als Priester, Agni, und als w├╝nschenswerthen Gast, als holden Freund dich f├╝r das himmlische Geschlecht.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдЬреАрд╡ ! рддреВ рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреБрдЭрдХреЛ (рднреГрдЧрд╡рдГ) рдкрд░рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╡ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реЗрд╖реБ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдЬрдиреЗрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХреЗ (рдЪрд╛рд░реБрдореН) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк (рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рд░рдпрд┐рдореН) рдзрди рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдореН) рджрд╛рдирд╢реАрд▓ (рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдореН) рдЕрдирд┐рдпрдд рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рджреЗрд╣-рджреЗрд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрд░ рдФрд░ рд╕реНрдерд╛рди-рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрддрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрд╣рд╛рд░рд╛ (рд╡рд░реЗрдгреНрдпрдореН) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рд╢реЗрд╡рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрд░реВрдк рдЬреАрд╡ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХреЗ (рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдп) рд╢реБрджреНрдз (рдЬрдиреНрдордиреЗ) рдЬрдиреНрдо рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди) рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢ рддреБрдЭ рдХреЛ (рдЖрджрдзреБрдГ) рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрд╕реА рдХреЛ рдЬреАрд╡ рдЬрд╛рди рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореА рддрдерд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рдЬреАрд╡ рдХреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рднреГрдЧрд╡реЛ рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реЗрд╖реБ рдЬрдиреЗрднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд░реБрдВ рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рдВ рд░рдпрд┐рдВ рди рдзрдирдорд┐рд╡ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдорддрд┐рдерд┐рдВ рд╡рд░реЗрдгреНрдпрдВ рд╢реЗрд╡рдВ рд▓рдмреНрдзреНрд╡рд╛ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдп рдЬрдиреНрдордиреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдорд┐рд╡ рддреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╜рджрдзреБрд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рдЬреАрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрд╣рд┐ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI worship with oblations that Agni whom the seven invoking priests invite as the invoker of the gods; who is most worthy of worship at sacrifices, and who is the donor of all riches; I solicit of him wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whom the seven tongues, whom the cantors choose as Hotar, best sacrificing at the ceremonies,
to Agni, the nave of all goods, I render service with a pleasurable
offering. I beg for a treasure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬseven tonguesтАЭ (sapt├б juhv├ас╕е) are somewhat puzzling, or rather the phrase has several possible interpretations. Renou takes it as a тАЬpr├й-bahuvr─лhiтАЭ (probably better expressed as тАЬde-composedтАЭ bahuvr─лhi), referring to the priests тАЬhaving seven offering ladlesтАЭ (juh┼л╠Б- meaning both тАШtongueтАЩ and тАШladleтАЩ); it is, of course, also possible to take the ladles as subject without reference to an underlying bahuvr─лhi (so Oldenberg SBE, Geldner), since inanimate things often have agency in the RV. But the other meaning тАШtongueтАЩ could also be meant literally (either in a de-composed bahuvr─лhi or not): (priests having) seven tongues, that is seven voices devoted to praising Agni.

See GeldnerтАЩs n. (also Witzel Got┼Н). This interpretation would make the first p─Бda semantically parallel with the second, where тАШcantorsтАЩ (v─Бgh├бtaс╕е) is the subject. And I will add another, more distant possibility, but one that makes better sense of the тАШsevenтАЩ - viz., the seven rivers or streams. The seven rivers are credited with giving birth to and nourishing Agni in a mystical passage in III.1.3-6, where they are also identified as seven v─Б╠Бс╣З─лс╕е тАШvoicesтАЩ (III.1.6d). Seven is a number especially characteristic of rivers, and since rivers are often said to be noisy (indeed the word nad─л╠Б- тАШriverтАЩ is derived from the root тИЪnad тАШroar), calling the rivers тАЬseven tonguesтАЭ here would fit semantically. In the end I donтАЩt think that choosing one of these possibilities and eliminating the others is the right strategy; the phrase is meant to be multivalent, evoking a number of features of the ritual context.

Griffith

Agni, the seven tongues’ deftest Sacrificer, him whom the priests elect at solemn worship,
The Herald, messenger of all the Vasus, I serve with dainty food, I ask for riches.

Oldenberg

I worship with good cheer Agni the steward 1 of all treasures, whom the seven ladles 2 (of the priests), the worshippers choose as the Hotri, the best sacrificer at the rites, and I pray for treasure 3.

Geldner

Denn die sieben Zungen, den die Priester als bestopfernden bei den Opfern zum Hotri erw├дhlen, den Agni, den Wagenlenker aller G├╢tter, pflege ich mit Labung; ihn bitte ich um Belohnung.

Grassmann

Der sieben L├╢ffel bestens weiht, den Priester, den sich die Beter bei den Opfern w├дhlen, Den Agni, welcher allen G├╢ttern dienet, verehr’ mit Tr├дnken ich und bitt’ um Schatz ihn.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSon of strength, favourably-shining Agni, grant to your worshipper on this occasion uninterrupted felicity; offspring of food, preserve him who praises you from sin with guards of metal.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O son of strength with the might of Mitra, today hold out unbroken shelters to us, your praisers.
O Agni, child of nourishment, deliver the singer from narrow straits, with your metal strongholds. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Vs. 9 is essentially a paraphrase of vs. 8, with several parallel expressions.

And the final p─Бda of 9 is the Nodhas refrain.

Griffith

Grant, Son of Strength, thou rich in friends, a refuge without a flaw this day to us thy praisers.
O Agni, Son of Strength, with forts of iron preserve thou from distress the man who lauds thee.

Oldenberg

Son of strength, great like Mitra, grant to-day flawless protection to us who magnify thee, Agni! guard from distress with strongholds of iron him who praises thee, O offspring of vigour!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVariously-shining Agni, be a shelter to him who praises you; be prosperity, Maghavan, to the wealthy (offerers of oblations); protect, Agni, your worshipper from sin; may Agni, who is rich with righteous acts, come (to us) quickly in the morning.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Maghavan = Indra; also, an epithet of Agni; lit. possessor of riches

Vs. 9 is essentially a paraphrase of vs. 8, with several parallel expressions.

And the final p─Бda of 9 is the Nodhas refrain.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ рдХрд┐ рдЬреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдзрд░реНрдо рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирдп рд╕реЗ рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреЛ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рджреЗрдХрд░ рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕реА рдХреЛ рд╕рднрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее реп рее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордШрд╡рдиреНрдирдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдБрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ рдордШрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд░реВрдердВ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡реЛ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдп рд╢рд░реНрдо рдЪ рдЧреГрдгрдиреНрддрдордВрд╣рд╕реЛ рдордХреНрд╖реВрд░реБрд╖реНрдп рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рддреНрд╡рдордкреНрдпрдВрд╣рд╕рдГ рдкреГрдердЧреНрднрд╡ рдпреЛ рдзрд┐рдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реБрд░реЗрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрддреНрддреЗ, рд╕ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рдЬрдЧрдореНрдпрд╛рджреН рднреГрд╢рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рд╕рднреЗрд╢рдГ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рднрд╡) (рд╡рд░реВрдердореН) рдЧреГрд╣рдореНред рд╡рд░реВрдердорд┐рддрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрей.рек) (рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ) рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдиреН рдХреАрд░реНрддрдпрддреЗ (рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдп (рднрд╡) рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрднрдпрддреНрд░ рджреНрд╡реНрдпрдЪреЛрд╜рддрд╕реНрддрд┐рдЩ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдордШрд╡рдиреН) рдкрд░рдордзрдирд╡рдиреН (рдордШрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ (рд╢рд░реНрдо) рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рдЙрд░реБрд╖реНрдп) рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЕрдВрд╣рд╕рдГ) рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рддреН (рдЧреГрдгрдиреНрддрдореН) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН (рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГ) рджрд┐рдирд╛рд░рдореНрднреЗ (рдордХреНрд╖реБ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдореНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЛрдЪрд┐ рддреБрдиреБреж (рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрд╛режрем.рей.резрейрей) рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реБрдГ) рдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрд┐рддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдГ (рдЬрдЧрдореНрдпрд╛рддреН) рднреГрд╢рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН рее реп рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░реНрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд┐рдирдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдпреЗрддреН, рд╕ рдПрд╡ рд╕рднрд╛рджреНрдпрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдГ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдГ рее реп рее редрдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрдмреЛрдзреНрдпрд╛ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди рдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд┐рдВрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирдореНрд░рддреЗрдиреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрд▓рд╛ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рджреЗрдКрди рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддреЛ. рддреНрдпрд╛рд▓рд╛рдЪ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рднрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдЪрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реп рее
